The math only checks out if a 1m*1m*1m block of tnt is energetically equivalent to a block of tnt the same size in real life. When the game was made the power of TNT was given arbitrary numbers for the blast radius and power. Some nerds somewhere on the internet figured out that 1 block of tnt is equivalent to 4.2 megajoules and that is equivalent to about 1kg of TNT IRL. So going by this math Wunba would have to make the TNT 1650 times bigger to get the energetic equivalent of a nuke. That said, even what he did was insanity. He made all these machines to streamline TNT production and made the volumetric equivalent of TNT as a whole ass nuke. In hardcore mode nonetheless. What he made is a very good representation of how big a cube of TNT would have to be in real life for it to have the same power as a nuke. Would be interesting to see this blow up if there was a mod installed that made each block of tnt 1650 times more powerful so it really is equivalent to a nukes worth of TNT.

Doing the calculations for the kilotons of TNT used, one TNT block is One meter cubed of TNT, which is essentially 1,650 kilograms of TNT, since there's 1.3 million blocks, we just do 1,650 x 1,300,000 which comes to 2145000000 kilograms of TNT, since nuclear weapons are typically measured in kilotons of TNT, this becomes 2145 kilotons, which becomes 2.145 megatons, just shy of the 57 megatons used in the Tsar Bomba (world's most powerful nuclear weapon), anywho, if we were to make a Minecraft bomb larger than the Tsar Bomba, Wunba would need 57 million subscribers, SO LETS MAKE IT HAPPEN PEOPLE!

Okay, let me break down 18:43 for ya.  "The VGA card is not supported by UEFI driver": Your computer is confused on what the GPU (VGA card) is. Fix: Remove the GPU and try integrated graphics. "CSM (Compatibility Support Module) settings have been changed for better compatibility": Setting your computer to boot the old fashioned way and using fallback VGA drivers. (y'know, 'cause the GPU is broken). When you remove your GPU, remember to reset BIOS settings. "Your system has POSTed in safe mode": First failed boot: because you held the power button to shut it down. Subsequent boots: because your last boot did not boot the system  PS. A POST is a Power On Self Test-- it checks how the system is working.  ---- Here's what happens on boot (maybe) ----- Motherboard: "Good morning M.2_1. What are you?" M.2_1: "I'm a Corsair MP600 Pro NH." Motherboard: "Thank you. SATA_0???? HELLO?" SATA_0: *does not exist* Motherboard: "Okay." Motherboard: "RAM module 0?" RAM module 0: "Here and I'm [n] gigabytes." Motherboard: "RAM module 1?" RAM module 1: "Here and I'm [n] gigabytes." Motherboard: "GPU?" GPU: "I'm a yyyyyyyyyyyy and my driver is 0xffffffffff in your dictionary of UEFI drivers." Motherboard: "That's not right. STOP THE POST!" *displays error*  EDIT1: Hey wait. I think your GPU was dead too. EDIT1: Also, wow. Thanks, but your "problem" you talked about is wrong. The motherboard would fry NOTHING or EVERYTHING on a single voltage rail. And it would actually be your PSU that's the culprit in that case.

For the song, I'm guessing either Final Countdown or Katy Perry's Firework. If you are wondering, I'm commenting as I watch
1. Your PC is a prebuild - contact a custom PC maker (I build and don't charge very much at all for my labor, usually around $500 plus the parts desired).  2. Don't Overclock your builds if you aren't certain you know exactly what you are doing - it's more of an art than a science, just FYI... and usually unecessary these days with todays CPU/RAM/GPU options.  3. That was your UEFI (new BIOS) screen, probably due to a corrupted boot medium. You corrupted your OS by writing to it too much - you probably were running MC and your OS on an SSD, which has a finite amount of write endurance before it becomes unusable. Consider using a RAM-FS for Minecraft that has that many block updates (or a dedicated server that you don't need to maintain), and keep backups of your OS disk periodically.

19:13 You more than likely have your games (including your hardcore save) on your C drive, which holds your OS. The world more than likely got so big, it overloaded the storage and caused the OS to have issues booting. Hi! I doubt you'll ever read this, but in case you do, you should take a look at setting up a private Network Attached Storage (NAS) server with automatic backups of your important files in case of a catastrophic failure happening again in the future! That way even if you were to lose the main drive, you'll at least have those automatic backups set up on whatever intervals you decide to set them up on. There's other ways you can be more secure about your data with but that's the most crucial one. On top of having those backups, you can have the extra storage as mass-storage for footage (or whatever you might need to store long-term). The NAS is a good safety measure to have, but I hope you never need it!

Great work Wunba â¤  994 19 Wunba   Show more replies   @maral2014 4 days ago 13:40. It is a common misconception that a minecraft tnt block contains 1,650 kg of tnt.  A minecraft tnt block only contains 412.5 kilograms of tnt, assuming trinitrotoluene is the explosive material.   Let me explain:  In minecraft, a block of tnt is 16 pixels in all 3 dimensions, X, Y, and Z.  If we look at the top of the tnt block, we can see 16 individual tubes filled with explosives, they grey material. The red material is simply the packaging.  There are 100 centimetres in a metre. 1 minecraft block is 1 cubic metre. Each tube of actual explosives is only 2 pixels wide.   100 / 16 = 6.25cm.  1 pixel is 6.25 cm wide.  Finding the top surface area for one explosive tube:  2 x 6.25 = 12.5 12.5^2 = 156.25 cm^2.  Now, lets find the volume of one explosive tube, assuming they run the full height of the block, which is one metre:  100 x 156.25 = 15,625 cm^3.  Now, we get the volume for all 16 tubes.  16 x 15,625 = 250,000 cm^3  Now that we have the volume for all of the tubes, we can calculate the ACTUAL mass of all of the TNT in one minecraft block.   the density of TNT is 1.65 g/cm^3 1.65 x 250,000 = 412,500 grams of tnt. 412,500 / 1000 = 412.5 kilograms of tnt.  Now, what was the actual yield of all of the tnt in the video?  In the video, he states that the yield is 2,421 KT of tnt. We now know this to be false.  There are 1,372,032 blocks of tnt. We multiply this by the mass of tnt in one block, in tonnes.   1,372,032 x 0.4125 = 565,963.2 tonnes. 565,963.2 tonnes = 565.9632 kilotonnes  All of the tnt in the pile is actually only about 566 kilotonnes.   For context, the largest pure fission weapon tested by the USA was Ivy King, which had a yield of 500KT, 66 KT less powerful than the tnt pile created in this video. The largest nuclear bomb, the Tsar Bomb (which was thermonuclear), had a yield of 50 Megatonnes, aka 50,000 KT.   For anyone who got this far, sorry if I gave you a headache

For some reason Iâ€™m in the mood for maths. 1.3 million cubic meters of trinitrotoluene, each of which weighs approximately 1650kg. 1.3 million times 1650 = 2145000000 (2.145 billion kg or 2.145 megatons)   The nuclear weapons used at the end of WW2 - The Little Boy and the Fat Man - each had an approximated payload equivalent to 20000 tonnes or 15000 tonnes respectively, so the nuclear yield of the TNT cube is equivalent to 107.25 Fat Men, or 143 little boys  To compare to a modern nuclear weapon, however: The most powerful nuclear weapon ever detonated is the Tsar Bomba, coming in at approximately 50 megatons, making it equivalent to 23.31 times the payload of the cube.   Do with that information what you will. (Also, Iâ€™m doing this not having watched the video yet, cause I saw the video and felt a mathematical urge. Feel free to point out any stupidity as you will)

That's not mathematically accurate, it's just a fancy redstone contraption that basically activates a tnt which makes all the others explode. The problem with this is that almost 80% of tnts will fly up in the air, pushed by the other tnts, so their power will be wasted in air instead of being an active contribution to the damage. A mathematically accurate tnt would be like a tnt where ALL the tnts explode simultaneously, and this is achieved by making a contraption where the LEAST DELAYED tnt waits and explodes only when the MOST delayed tnt explodes.

Make sure the firmware is up to date on your new SSD. The Samsung 990 pro (and a couple similarly specced/priced drives) have a firmware bug that kills that crazy fast. Also, never fill your SSD more than 80-90% full, cuz that also kills them faster.  Also, backups don't have to be complicated. You can set up an automatic Google drive share, or OneDrive, Dropbox, etc, and set it to run for example every day at 5am. Or you can go hard mode and keep a local backup somewhere else in your house, but there's some open source tools to do that easier too.

The fact that the PC technician didn't tell you it's the mother board tells me he's either not good at his job, or he wants to make more money from you. SSD's last about 10 years if you don't use it to write, delete and rewrite all the time. SSD lifespans are determined by read and write cycles, and most SSD's can be rewritten completely over 100 times their capacities, so it takes years. SSD failure, especially after long usage from a reputable brand, usually indicates that something else is wrong.

So my ADHD brain was curious to see how badly your SSD screwed itself over:  The Samsung 990 Pro SSD has a little over 6.9kmb/sec read/write speed. 1 non-storage Minecraft block takes up about 2.5 bytes in each region file. You placed about 1728 blocks (1 shulker is 27 slots x 64 blocks) in about 26 seconds for ~66.4615 blocks per second. This means your region files were changed at a rate of ~166.1538 bytes per second, for a total change of 0.04984mb per autosave interval (every 5 minutes). Even if you account for placing a shulker every few seconds, the total number of shulkers in each chunk with the 1.3M blocks inside, your player NBT changing from a variety of sources, and other random things, you really only created about 0.061883MB worth of updates from the project spread across the region files in your world.   To put into perspective, the 5 sand dupers and shulker loaders probably cause more writes per second with just entities being created and destroyed.  What does this mean? A project like this shouldn't have caused that SSD to fail unless your Motherboard and PSU combo decided to randomly fry it. Your motherboard was probably fine, the PSU is the failure point, and IDK how your repair shop didn't see why it failed.

I think your computer broke because it couldn't decide whether it had a Ryzen 9-5950X or an i9-14900K as the main CPU. That's kind of a crucial thing to get right. Probably could cause some SSD corruption seeing as the PCIe driver hardware tends to be onboard these days. Might be overclocking the memory something chronic as well, as it also can't decide if it's running DDR4-2666 or DDR5-4000.  Maybe something hooky in the motherboard BIOS? Which would then do bad things to the voltage supplies maybe.  BTW everyone, object lesson in the value of backups. Especially if you happen to habitually have a USB hard drive plugged in, which could fit the important parts of a 2TB main volume on it many times over and only need a few hours to fully duplicate. (Could the computer guy not have recovered your stuff onto a less volatile medium, so if the new SSD suffered infant mortality it could be duplicated straight onto another replacement?)  ...reminds me, I'm overdue to take an offline copy of my own recent files. 13:40. It is a common misconception that a minecraft tnt block contains 1,650 kg of tnt.  A minecraft tnt block only contains 412.5 kilograms of tnt, assuming trinitrotoluene is the explosive material.   Let me explain:  In minecraft, a block of tnt is 16 pixels in all 3 dimensions, X, Y, and Z.  If we look at the top of the tnt block, we can see 16 individual tubes filled with explosives, they grey material. The red material is simply the packaging.  There are 100 centimetres in a metre. 1 minecraft block is 1 cubic metre. Each tube of actual explosives is only 2 pixels wide.   100 / 16 = 6.25cm.  1 pixel is 6.25 cm wide.  Finding the top surface area for one explosive tube:  2 x 6.25 = 12.5 12.5^2 = 156.25 cm^2.  Now, lets find the volume of one explosive tube, assuming they run the full height of the block, which is one metre:  100 x 156.25 = 15,625 cm^3.  Now, we get the volume for all 16 tubes.  16 x 15,625 = 250,000 cm^3  Now that we have the volume for all of the tubes, we can calculate the ACTUAL mass of all of the TNT in one minecraft block.   the density of TNT is 1.65 g/cm^3 1.65 x 250,000 = 412,500 grams of tnt. 412,500 / 1000 = 412.5 kilograms of tnt.  Now, what was the actual yield of all of the tnt in the video?  In the video, he states that the yield is 2,421 KT of tnt. We now know this to be false.  There are 1,372,032 blocks of tnt. We multiply this by the mass of tnt in one block, in tonnes.   1,372,032 x 0.4125 = 565,963.2 tonnes. 565,963.2 tonnes = 565.9632 kilotonnes  All of the tnt in the pile is actually only about 566 kilotonnes.   For context, the largest pure fission weapon tested by the USA was Ivy King, which had a yield of 500KT, 66 KT less powerful than the tnt pile created in this video. The largest nuclear bomb, the Tsar Bomb (which was thermonuclear), had a yield of 50 Megatonnes, aka 50,000 KT.   For anyone who got this far, sorry if I gave you a headache.

Here's a wiki of Tsar Bomb if you don't believe: https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tsar_Bomba  To calculate all that, you'll need to use Trinity (the Oppenheimer Bomb, which has 25 kilotons of TNT) (wiki: https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trinity_(nuclear_test) ), then use the calculator, multiply 25 by 130 (as Wumba said, his explosion is 130 times larger), then convert it into megatons (this link: https://www.google.com/search?q=kilotons+to+megatons&rlz=1C1VDKB_enCA985CA985&oq=kilotons+to+megatons&gs_lcrp=EgZjaHJvbWUyBggAEEUYOdIBCDY1NjdqMGoxqAIAsAIA&sourceid=chrome&ie=UTF-8 ) then finally you can divide the Tsar Bomb's power by that you've got.  P.S Hi Wumba! So I was curious about this so I did some math! Doing some quick research, several people have done calculations and the most precise I could find (using the actual density of tnt) puts Minecraft tnt at a weight of around 1,650 kg (about 2 lbs) this is 1.65 metric tons (explosives are typically measured in tons of tnt) multiplying this 1.65 by the 1,331,000 tnt Wunba is going to place you get 2,196,150 tons of tnt. Converting this to megatons, you get 2.19615 megatons, lets just round this up to 2.2 mt. For some context, the Gadget, Fat Man, and Little Boy were all measured in terms of KILOtons, you donâ€™t typically start getting into MEGAtons until you get to explosions like those caused by a Super. So yes, Wunba has made a bomb more powerful than most atomic bombs! (Bonus: according to the nukemap website, this put Wunbas weapon somewhere between the B-83 and the R-12 (SS-4) in terms of power)
